  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ce3ccfe2-6648-4d9c-a3e9-c14f13822974'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

      initAppleId();

      initializeSiwa();

<span id="freeTextContainer12869564126846654637"><br/>Dear Mr. Vaughan, <br/><br/>I do not know what process you go though to produce comics like these. I do not know what dark alchemy you perform, what infernal pacts you have agreed to, what terrifying drugs you must imbibe. I have no idea what arcane rituals you must perform every day, what odd odd habits of diet and exorcize you must maintain to keep your mind limber and sparking, to write things like this. <br/><br/>I just wanted to say, whatever it is you're doing, please keep doing it. <br/><br/>Sincerely, <br/><br/>pat<br/></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer11870129680443229709"><b>3.5/5</b><br/>This volume found what I felt was missing in the first: backstory and a lot of heart.<br/>We learned more about Marko's past and how he and Alana met. I love him. So much. <br/>I also enjoyed getting to know the new characters, Marko's parents and Gwendolyn, as they helped flesh out the story and provided some of my favorite moments.<br/>Fiona Staples' illustrations did not fail me. They were so vivid - sometimes to a gross degree when it came to certain creatures.<br/>I'm getting more used to the style of thi</span>
  <span id="freeText11870129680443229709" style="display:none"><b>3.5/5</b><br />This volume found what I felt was missing in the first: backstory and a lot of heart.<br />We learned more about Marko's past and how he and Alana met. I love him. So much. <br />I also enjoyed getting to know the new characters, Marko's parents and Gwendolyn, as they helped flesh out the story and provided some of my favorite moments.<br />Fiona Staples' illustrations did not fail me. They were so vivid - sometimes to a gross degree when it came to certain creatures.<br />I'm getting more used to the style of this series. It's vulgar and abrasive, but there is real love at the center of it (though it's sometimes hard to see).<br />Can't wait to see what is to come!</span>

    <a title="Federico DN" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/29005117-federico-dn"><img alt="Federico DN" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1478986000p2/29005117.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2947538761?book_show_action=true">Aug 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Federico DN" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Federico DN" href="/user/show/29005117-federico-dn">Federico DN</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29005117-federico-dn?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/29005117-federico-dn?shelf=almost-fav">almost-fav</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2947538761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8189689365953659806">Tender lovebirds, and not so tender bounty-hunters.<br/><br/>In this continuation of the series we backtrack to the early days when Alana, the soldier, and Marko, the prisoner, met, and how everything unfolded for them to be together. From an indifferent beating to a crazy incomprehensible love; while at the present time also fleeing Cleave from their many pursuers, and trying to find some place in the universe, any place at all, where their little baby daughter can be safe.<br/><br/>Excellent sequel to Saga. I enj</span>
  <span id="freeText8189689365953659806" style="display:none">Tender lovebirds, and not so tender bounty-hunters.<br /><br />In this continuation of the series we backtrack to the early days when Alana, the soldier, and Marko, the prisoner, met, and how everything unfolded for them to be together. From an indifferent beating to a crazy incomprehensible love; while at the present time also fleeing Cleave from their many pursuers, and trying to find some place in the universe, any place at all, where their little baby daughter can be safe.<br /><br />Excellent sequel to Saga. I enjoyed it even much more than #1, and looking forward to reading the next chapters. Did I ever say I'm a sucker for love stories?<br /><br />Until next time,<br /><br />-----------------------------------------------<br /><br />Tiernos amorcitos, y no tan tiernos cazarrecompenzas.<br /><br />En esta continuación de la serie volvemos atrás a los primeros días cuando Alana, la soldado, y Marko, el prisionero, se conocieron, y cómo todo se desarrolló para que terminaran juntos. Desde una paliza indiferente hasta un loco amor incomprendido; mientras a su vez en el tiempo presente escapan de Cleave y sus muchos perseguidores, y tratando de hallar algún lugar en el universo, cualquier lugar posible, donde su pequeña hija bebé pueda estar segura.<br /><br />Excelente secuela de Saga. La disfruté incluso mucho más que #1, y entusiasmado por leer los próximos capítulos. Alguna vez dije que soy fan de las historias de amor?<br /><br />Hasta la próxima,</span>
  <a data-text-id="8189689365953659806" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1346222653?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

          added it




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=comics">comics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=adult">adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1346222653" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3538830444959522664"><b>
  <i>‘‘Never worry what other people think of you, because no one ever thinks of you.’’</i>
</b><br/><br/>Give me an S! Give me an A! Give me a G! How about another A?<br/><br/>… SAGA all the way. Oh man, I was never <i>that</i> into comics. Sure, there’s a couple I came to enjoy, such as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20898019.Ms__Marvel__Vol__1_No_Normal' title='Ms. Marvel, Vol. 1 No Normal by G. Willow Wilson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Ms. Marvel, Vol. 1: No Normal</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17671993.Injustice_Gods_Among_Us_Year_One__Vol__1' title='Injustice Gods Among Us Year One, Vol. 1 by Tom Taylor' rel='nofollow noopener'>Injustice: Gods Among Us, Vol. 1</a>, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23093359.The_Wicked___The_Divine__Vol__1_The_Faust_Act' title='The Wicked + The Divine, Vol. 1 The Faust Act by Kieron Gillen' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Wicked + The Divine, Vol. 1: The Faust Act</a>… but I never felt so attached to that of a bundle of characters in a same series. I’m thinking, and thinking, and truth is that I love </span>
  <span id="freeText3538830444959522664" style="display:none"><b>
  <i>‘‘Never worry what other people think of you, because no one ever thinks of you.’’</i>
</b><br><br>Give me an S! Give me an A! Give me a G! How about another A?<br><br>… SAGA all the way. Oh man, I was never <i>that</i> into comics. Sure, there’s a couple I came to enjoy, such as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20898019.Ms__Marvel__Vol__1_No_Normal" title="Ms. Marvel, Vol. 1 No Normal by G. Willow Wilson" rel="nofollow noopener">Ms. Marvel, Vol. 1: No Normal</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/17671993.Injustice_Gods_Among_Us_Year_One__Vol__1" title="Injustice Gods Among Us Year One, Vol. 1 by Tom Taylor" rel="nofollow noopener">Injustice: Gods Among Us, Vol. 1</a>, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23093359.The_Wicked___The_Divine__Vol__1_The_Faust_Act" title="The Wicked + The Divine, Vol. 1 The Faust Act by Kieron Gillen" rel="nofollow noopener">The Wicked + The Divine, Vol. 1: The Faust Act</a>… but I never felt so attached to that of a bundle of characters in a same series. I’m thinking, and thinking, and truth is that I love every one of them. Alright, so I mayhap want to dispatch of that annoying robot prince, but I’m sure he’ll slaughter himself some day, and I’m pretty patient. Well, relatively patient.<br><br>Did I ever mention how much I love the fact that it is the lovebirds’ little Hazel who narrates the story? I can’t wait to see her all grown up. This sequel is different from the first book because it doesn’t only go on with the plot and how things were left but also goes back in time to moments that led to the present, and I must say that I was HOOKED.<br><br><b>Best comic ever.</b><br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437856r/885246._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="220" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

          </span>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2304664882" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13508613270889717894">Saga is just superb. Aside from the cool characters, its general weirdness and unflinching nature, it also recognises the power of words:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467846618i/19637406._SY540_.jpg' width='200' height='500' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And for me that’s rather important. This particular book has caused the entire situation, pushing the characters to sue for piece in a world driven by hatred and war. The book made them fall in love with each other, and give birth to a new future that they now must fight to protect: a baby born from a union between two races that have always hated each other:<br/><br/> <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519310815i/25104451._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='300' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> </span>
  <span id="freeText13508613270889717894" style="display:none">Saga is just superb. Aside from the cool characters, its general weirdness and unflinching nature, it also recognises the power of words:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467846618i/19637406._SY540_.jpg" width="200" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And for me that’s rather important. This particular book has caused the entire situation, pushing the characters to sue for piece in a world driven by hatred and war. The book made them fall in love with each other, and give birth to a new future that they now must fight to protect: a baby born from a union between two races that have always hated each other:<br><br> <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519310815i/25104451._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>So the plot is rather fantastic with so much potential, I really look forward to seeing where this all goes though I do wonder if it will lose some of its shock factor. There’s been a lot of strange characters/monster so far. <br><br><b>Can it get any weirder?</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1519311011i/25104465._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="500" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1513478118i/24693460._SX540_.png" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1475970237i/20788533._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Time will tell.</span>

<div id="review_2933937874" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2933937874" />
    <a title="Richard" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/73431206-richard"><img alt="Richard" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1525868884p2/73431206.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2933937874?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Richard" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Richard" href="/user/show/73431206-richard">Richard</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/73431206-richard?shelf=graphic-novel">graphic-novel</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2933937874" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17099042031153407019">The second book in this graphic novel series by Brian K.Vaughan (writer) and Fiona Staples (artist) is as good as the first ….…. maybe even better, as we continue to get to know the main characters.<br/>It’s bursting with mad invention, wonderfully evocative artwork, a story that is developing nicely and an ever growing cast of very strange characters.<br/>Marko and Alana, the star-crossed lovers (from both sides of a planetary conflict) and their child Hazel, continue their escape from a ragbag assortmen</span>
  <span id="freeText17099042031153407019" style="display:none">The second book in this graphic novel series by Brian K.Vaughan (writer) and Fiona Staples (artist) is as good as the first ….…. maybe even better, as we continue to get to know the main characters.<br />It’s bursting with mad invention, wonderfully evocative artwork, a story that is developing nicely and an ever growing cast of very strange characters.<br />Marko and Alana, the star-crossed lovers (from both sides of a planetary conflict) and their child Hazel, continue their escape from a ragbag assortment of assassins, bounty hunters and ex lovers. <br />In this episode we find a planet that’s a baby, an organic spacecraft, a lying cat, a telepathic child rescued from a brothel planet and Marko’s very disapproving parents. Not forgetting one of my favourite characters, Hazel’s teenage babysitter, the disemboweled and very cool ghost Izabel!<br />There’s wisecracking humour, pathos and an exciting adventure that’s impossible to second guess.. <br />All very modern, quite adult and bizarre.<br />You can probably guess I’m enjoying this series very much!<br />I’ve included a link to my review of Saga Vol.1 below:<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2663942813">https://www.goodreads.com/review/show...</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17099042031153407019" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer680220867" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3455743689926501751">A couple of star-crossed lovers from two different species on opposing sides of an interstellar war are on the run in a wooden rocket ship with their infant daughter and her ghost babysitter as they are pursued by the forces of both sides including a royal family member who is a robot with a television for a head as well as a bounty hunter who has an oversized cat who can tell when anyone is lying. <br/><br/>Geez, why can’t any comic book creators come up with something original?<br/><br/>Ah, but seriously…. This s</span>
  <span id="freeText3455743689926501751" style="display:none">A couple of star-crossed lovers from two different species on opposing sides of an interstellar war are on the run in a wooden rocket ship with their infant daughter and her ghost babysitter as they are pursued by the forces of both sides including a royal family member who is a robot with a television for a head as well as a bounty hunter who has an oversized cat who can tell when anyone is lying. <br /><br />Geez, why can’t any comic book creators come up with something original?<br /><br />Ah, but seriously…. This second volume of Brian K. Vaughan’s wild story is just as good as the first. One of the things I love most about this series so far is that despite all the crazy elements, Vaughan makes everything so relatable. This may be taking place in space during a massive war that involves everything from magic to worlds dedicated solely to prostitution, but whether it’s meeting the in-laws or telling us about how Alana and Marko met, there’s a very human element to all the wackiness. That’s what makes the whole thing so damn awesome.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3455743689926501751" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer605668021311110208"><b>Actual rating</b>: a low 3.5 stars.<br/><br/><b>Okay</b>, so I'm not nearly as <b>enthusiastic</b> about this one as I was about volume 1 ← <i>this might (or might not) be the understatement of the century.</i> <br/><br/><b>Volume 1</b> left me feeling like this:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457938528ra/18423635.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Yes, I am a cigarette smoking dude with a moustache and over-gelled hair in real life.</i><br/><br/><b>This volume?</b> It left me feeling like this:<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457938528i/18423636.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Yes, I am also a freaky-eyed sausage on paws in real life.   <span id="freeText605668021311110208" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating</b>: a low 3.5 stars.<br><br><b>Okay</b>, so I'm not nearly as <b>enthusiastic</b> about this one as I was about volume 1 ← <i>this might (or might not) be the understatement of the century.</i> <br><br><b>Volume 1</b> left me feeling like this:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1457938528ra/18423635.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Yes, I am a cigarette smoking dude with a moustache and over-gelled hair in real life.</i><br><br><b>This volume?</b> It left me feeling like this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457938528i/18423636.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Yes, I am also a freaky-eyed sausage on paws in real life. I am so cool.</i><br><br><b>But I am not</b> <s>completely</s> insane <s>yet </s>. I didn't give this book a 3.5-star rating just because 3.5 is a pretty number. It isn't. A pretty number, I mean. Because odd numbers suck. So ugly. Ew ew ew. Oops, am I digressing again? Thought so. <s>Too much vodka</s> Lack of coffee and all that crap. So. Why is this volume still <b>pretty awesome</b> but not quite you almost made it there I could I LOVED you but I didn't:<br><br>➊ <b>The Freaking Art is a Freaking Thing of Beauty</b>.<br><br>➽ The cover is perfection:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457940152i/18423704.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ And look at this:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457940152i/18423705.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457940152i/18423706.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>A thing of beauty</b>, I tell you. Fiona Staples' work is seriously amazing.<br><br>➋ <b>Super creative world and characters</b>. <br><br>➽ Me love me <b>Lying Cat</b>:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457942450i/18423936.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ <b>Izabel</b>, coolest ghost babysitter ever:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457942450i/18423935.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ <b>Gorillas</b> and stuff:<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1411483102i/11237004._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ Mostest awesomest <b>doctor</b> ever:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457942968i/18423976.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➌ <b>Awesome female characters</b>:<br><br>➽ <b>Alanna</b>:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457940698i/18423738.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ <b>Gwendolyn</b>:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457942450i/18423937.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➽ <b>Klara</b>:<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457954558i/18425298.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457954558i/18425299.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>➊ <b>The Romeo and Juliet vibe</b>:<br><br><b>Please kill me somebody</b>. Can't we just leave the <b>freaking romance</b> at the doorstep for once?! Sex is great but please don't ruin everything with <b>cute, silly scenes</b>.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457954169i/18425278.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>EW, EW, EW.<br><br>➋ <b>Little action and slow-paced, barely there plot </b>:<br><br>There are some <b>great individual scenes</b> here, but the storyline itself? Bleh. The whole "meet the in-laws" subplot feels like something <b>out of a sitcom</b>. The scenes featuring Alanna and Barr are <b>dull as hell</b>. The "let's get the baby sitter back" part of the plot isn't that bad, but it's still <b>pretty meh</b>. And it adds nothing to the story as a whole. The only subplot <b>I actually enjoyed</b> was the one involving The Will, Gwendolyn, Lying Cat, Sophie, etc. Too bad these guys aren't the <b>main characters</b> in the story.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457958091i/18425756.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457959259i/18425949.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1457958091i/18425758._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br> <br>»» <b>And the moral of this non-review is</b>: I'll probably give volume 3 a try, but if the authors keep doing the <b>more silly romance and family vs. less cool action and bloodshed</b> thing, I'm done. Yes, this is a threat. <b>Feel free to shudder now</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="605668021311110208" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_586633863" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/586633863" />
    <a title="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party"><img alt="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1562621595p2/10923016.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/586633863?book_show_action=true">Apr 10, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" class="user" itemprop="url" name="David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party" href="/user/show/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party">David - proud Gleeman in Branwen&#39;s adventuring party</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=graphic-novels-are-cool">graphic-novels-are-cool</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=space-opera">space-opera</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=sassy-queen-sarah-rules">sassy-queen-sarah-rules</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10923016-david---proud-gleeman-in-branwen-s-adventuring-party?shelf=science-fiction">science-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer586633863" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10968779694877807224"><i>Brian K Vaughan's epic </i><b>Saga</b><i> continues, as does the awesomeness from the first volume!</i><br/><br/>Lovers who each come from opposite sides of two warring worlds, Alana and Marko have become the symbol for a possible union between the planet Landfall and the moon of Wreath. However, since the governments of both Landfall and Wreath have no interest in making peace with each other, they have declared Alana & Marco to be a threat to their ways of life, and have each dispatched hunters to murder Alana & Marco be</span>
  <span id="freeText10968779694877807224" style="display:none"><i>Brian K Vaughan's epic </i><b>Saga</b><i> continues, as does the awesomeness from the first volume!</i><br><br>Lovers who each come from opposite sides of two warring worlds, Alana and Marko have become the symbol for a possible union between the planet Landfall and the moon of Wreath. However, since the governments of both Landfall and Wreath have no interest in making peace with each other, they have declared Alana &amp; Marco to be a threat to their ways of life, and have each dispatched hunters to murder Alana &amp; Marco before their story can inspire others to seek out a peaceful union as well. Not interested in being enslaved by the politics of their respective worlds, Alana &amp; Marco continue to escape their pursuers so they can raise their daughter Hazel in peace. But now, they face threats internally as well as externally. In addition to the ruthless bounty hunter known as The Will, and the chillingly methodical soldier Prince Robot IV, Alana and Marco find themselves pursued by even more obsessed hunters...Marco's parents! Horrified that Marco has "betrayed" their people, the misguided couple have found their son and are determined to convince Marco to abandon his new family in order to honor his old one? In a universe ravaged by war, can the love between two people still survive?<br><br>Since I've pretty much read almost everything Brian K Vaughan has ever written, you'd think he would have run out of ways to astonish me by now, but no, once again Mr. Vaughan (aided by the eye-popping visuals provided by artist Fiona Staples) hasmanaged to blow me away! The intrigue starts right away with the arrival of Marco's parents. The previous edition of <i>"Saga"</i> focused more on how the battle between their people was impacting Marco and Alana, but now Vaughan adds even more gravitas to the horrors of war by showing not only how it affects individuals, but also how it can potentially destroy families as well. Marco's mother's hostility towards Alana paint a grim picture of how even the people closest to us can have their minds poisoned by prejudiced. And not content to simply use Marco's parents to tell ONE amazing story, Marco's father opens the door to an equally compelling subplot. Even more impressive is that while tackling such heavy themes, Vaughan still manages to inject enough levity to make the material as much fun as it is moving. Just as things start to feel a little too somber, someone (often Alana) will come up with an amusing remark that instantly lightens the mood...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417090i/824619._SX540_.jpg" width="399" height="275" alt="saga1" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>One thing that amazed me about <i>Saga's</i> first volume was how the supporting characters were just as interesting as Marco &amp; Alana, and that hasn't changed this time around. The moral quandary that bounty hunter The Will found himself in previously is explored further, but this time he finds some unexpected help from Marco's bitter ex-fiance, Gwendolyn. Gwendolyn proves to be a perfect partner for The Will, as her intelligence and craftiness only enhances The Will's terrifying physical powers. Gwendolyn's former relationship with Marco adds a personal element to the duo's quest to capture the star-crossed lovers, and with her on board, The Will's journey proves to be every bit as mesmerizing as Marco &amp; Alana's! In addition, some much needed laughs are provided by The Will's pet, a cat who's compelled to call out anyone who tells a lie...even when it's The Will himself!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417090i/824620.jpg" width="399" height="399" alt="saga2" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>But out of all these great characters, my favorite still remains Izabel, the disembodied spirit of a dead teenage girl who now acts as a kind of "spiritual babysitter" for Alana and Marko's baby, Hazel. Izabel's perkiness and attitude reminds me of another brilliant Brian K Vaughan character, Molly from <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7389.Runaways__Vol__1_Pride_and_Joy" title="Runaways, Vol. 1 Pride and Joy by Brian K. Vaughan" rel="nofollow noopener">Runaways, Vol. 1: Pride and Joy</a>. Despite her rather frightening appearance and her sad history, Izabel remains a ray of sunshine in an often bleak world, with her spirit <i>(no pun intended)</i> and good cheer making her a ghost who's far too lovable to be scary!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417090i/824621._SY540_.jpg" width="399" height="340" alt="saga3" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Now, despite my enthusiasm for everything I've talked about above, I still haven't even mention my <i>favorite</i> part of Volume 2! That would be a self-contained chapter where another one of Alana &amp; Marco's pursuers, Prince Robot IV, visits an author Alana admires in hopes that the writer may hold some clue as to where his fan may have fled to. On paper, this may sound like a rather dull pit-stop, as almost the entirety of the issue is dedicated to the Prince's conversation with author D Oswald Heist. However, their conversation proves to be one of the most compelling elements in this volume. The Prince and Heist engage in a rather weighty philosophical debate that covers many topics, including the value and true meaning of art, the importance of loyalty, fatherhood, and the price of war. While the Prince had displayed less personality than most of the other characters up until now, in this issue we learn much more about what truly drives him, and that knowledge transforms him into quite possibly the most dangerous threat yet to Alana and Marco! In addition, we learn more about the author whose work may or may not be indirectly responsible for Alana's willingness to break free from her own people...<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380417090i/824622._SX540_.jpg" width="399" height="275" alt="saga4" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><i>This is most certainly NOT Brian K Vaughan talking about "Saga"!</i><br><br><b>DAVE'S FINAL JUDGMENT - </b><br><br><i>
  <b>THE DEFENSE</b>
</i><br> - Deep and enthralling story and world-building <br> - Main characters and secondary characters are equally captivating <br> - Extremely clever and often amusing dialogue <br> - Fascinating philosophical themes are explored<br> - Absolutely no filler or padding, Vaughan and Staples make every panel count<br><br><i>
  <b>THE PROSECUTION</b>
</i><br> - Strong language and sexually explicit situations may turn off gentler readers <br> - Won't be nearly as satisfying unless you've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/15704307.Saga__Volume_1" title="Saga, Volume 1 by Brian K. Vaughan" rel="nofollow noopener">Saga, Volume 1</a> first <br><br><i>
  <b>THE VERDICT</b>
</i><br>Just as brilliant and exciting as the first volume, this edition further cements Saga's potential to be one of the greatest graphic novel stories of all time! <br></span>
  <a data-text-id="10968779694877807224" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer4085928099725721487">MY BLOG: <a href='http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/02/saga-volume-two-brian-k-vaughan-fiona.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br/><br/>OMG! I loved this one even better than the first, although, there is one monster that will give nightmares for some time. You will see :-D<br/><br/>So Marko's parents get beamed on board and they are not happy to see that he married Alana who is supposed to be an enemy of their race. <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456624188i/18258728.jpg' alt=' : ' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>And, when they get there, Marko's mom banishes our wonderful ghost friend Izabel. Soooooo.... Marko goes off through the portal to find her and his mom follows him. This leaves Alana, Mar</span>
  <span id="freeText4085928099725721487" style="display:none">MY BLOG: <a href="http://melissa413readsalot.blogspot.com/2016/02/saga-volume-two-brian-k-vaughan-fiona.html" rel="nofollow noopener">Melissa Martin's Reading List</a><br><br>OMG! I loved this one even better than the first, although, there is one monster that will give nightmares for some time. You will see :-D<br><br>So Marko's parents get beamed on board and they are not happy to see that he married Alana who is supposed to be an enemy of their race. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456624188i/18258728.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>And, when they get there, Marko's mom banishes our wonderful ghost friend Izabel. Soooooo.... Marko goes off through the portal to find her and his mom follows him. This leaves Alana, Marko's dad Barr and little baby Hazel. They don't hit it off at first, well Alana is being a her normal self, but then they finally bond and she finds out a secret Barr has been keeping from his family. It's sad. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456624188i/18258729._SX540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Meanwhile..... Marko and mummy are dealing with this....<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456624188i/18258730.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Meet balls.. er.. I mean Fard. Lol, yeah I thought it said fart when I first read it and dear Lord. I have no words.. <br><br>Anyhoo..<br><br>We get to meet Gwendolyn in this book. She's the one that Marko jilted, he was engaged to her. She's not happy so she gets with the bounty hunter and his cat to go looking for him after they save the little girl. You have to read the first book to know what I'm talking about. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456624188i/18258731._SY540_.jpg" alt=" : " class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That Robot, I call TV HEAD is still looking for Alana, Marko and the baby too! All of these people want them! <br><br>I like that the book goes back and tells some back stories of how Alana and Marko met. They also show some backstory of Marko as a child. <br><br>The graphics are awesome once again, the story line is awesome, there is plenty of snark and crap being blown up, stabbed, gassed, shot and what not. I love these novels so far and look forward to the rest. <br></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_625473103" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/625473103" />
    <a title="Amanda" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda"><img alt="Amanda" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1411956191p2/1219253.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/625473103?book_show_action=true">May 26, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Amanda" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Amanda" href="/user/show/1219253-amanda">Amanda</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=kick-ass">kick-ass</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=blog">blog</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1219253-amanda?shelf=comics">comics</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer625473103" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17301648638723256291">In the first 6 issues of <i>Saga</i> (which comprised volume 1 of the trade edition), Brian K. Vaughan threw in enough weird ass shit to keep me in a delightfully perpetual state of "what the hell was that?" So much so that I worried the inventiveness might eventually wear thin, begin to feel as though it's trying too hard (as I sometimes feel with China Mieville's <i>Dial H</i>), or simply create such a labyrinthine mythology that it's just not worth trying to puzzle it all out. The second 6 issues have defi</span>
  <span id="freeText17301648638723256291" style="display:none">In the first 6 issues of <i>Saga</i> (which comprised volume 1 of the trade edition), Brian K. Vaughan threw in enough weird ass shit to keep me in a delightfully perpetual state of "what the hell was that?" So much so that I worried the inventiveness might eventually wear thin, begin to feel as though it's trying too hard (as I sometimes feel with China Mieville's <i>Dial H</i>), or simply create such a labyrinthine mythology that it's just not worth trying to puzzle it all out. The second 6 issues have definitely allayed those fears as they are as outrageous and genuine as the first story arc, losing none of the batshit craziness or heart.<br /><br />Hazel, the newborn daughter of Marko and Alana, continues to narrate the story of her parents from an unknown point in the future. Marko and Alana, both soldiers from two warring alien races, have a romance that reads like <i>Romeo and Juliet</i> on crack. On the run as fugitives from their respective races, they continue to search the universe for a safe place to live, love, and raise Hazel. But, alas, bounty hunters continue to plague them and, worst of all, the sudden appearance of ex-flames (an enraged Gwendolyn, Marko's one time fiancée) and in-laws (Marko's parents seek out their wayward child at the worst possible of times, complicating his escape with Alana).<br /><br />This arc provides background on several significant characters, including how Marko and Alana met, as well as the history of the relationship between The Will and The Stalk, the star-crossed (and bad ass) bounty hunters hot on their trail. For those uninitiated to Brian Vaughan's work, however, be forewarned: there will be sex scenes, giants with pendulous scrotums, and enough deviant behavior to make Sodom and Gomorrah blush with shame. However, I also appreciate the maturity with which the relationships are portrayed--they're real without being romanticized. <i>Saga</i> works beautifully because of this and because of the huge debt the series owes to illustrator Fiona Staples. The work of any other artist could have made Vaughan's ideas too cartoonish, too over-the-top, but Staples's work is the right mesh of quirky and realistic that roots this world in an organic quality that gives it weight and authenticity.<br /><br />In short, I can't praise <i>Saga</i> highly enough. It's a testament to what comics can achieve when writers and artists are let off the leashes of pre-conceived, "safe" concepts and allowed to chase after their most vivid, fevered imaginings. <br /><br />Cross posted at <a href="http://viiamanda.blogspot.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">This Insignificant Cinder</a> and at <a href="http://www.shelfinflicted.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Shelf Inflicted</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="17301648638723256291" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1644287873" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1644287873" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1644287873?book_show_action=true">May 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=graphic-novels">graphic-novels</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=dark">dark</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2016">read-in-2016</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=sci-fi">sci-fi</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1644287873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3670002838211082451"><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1644076193?book_show_action=false' rel='nofollow noopener'>Vol. 1</a> ★★★★<br/><br/>I completely loved this. I was enthralled the whole time learning about Hazel and the events that lead up to her creation. This world is so creative and imaginative that I'm just blown away. This is one of the best graphic-novels out, and my words won't do justice as to why I would recommend this to every living soul. <br/><br/>The main theme in this book is the blind prejudice that all these souls have grown up believing in, because it has always been forced upon them. Everyone can take someth</span>
  <span id="freeText3670002838211082451" style="display:none"><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1644076193?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Vol. 1</a> ★★★★<br><br>I completely loved this. I was enthralled the whole time learning about Hazel and the events that lead up to her creation. This world is so creative and imaginative that I'm just blown away. This is one of the best graphic-novels out, and my words won't do justice as to why I would recommend this to every living soul. <br><br>The main theme in this book is the blind prejudice that all these souls have grown up believing in, because it has always been forced upon them. Everyone can take something out of this lesson, especially with all the hate this election season is bringing. <br><br>Hazel being the narrator was such a genius move by Brian K. Vaughan. It is so expertly done, too. One minute you feel your heart being ripped out, the next Hazel is making you laugh out loud. Hazel's voice is perfect, and watching her journey is magical.<br><br>This bind-up gives us flashbacks from the past constantly. It's done very well, and helps the reader get a way better understand at what Marko and Alana have at stake and why it's so important that love wins. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380437856r/885246._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm now going to break down each chapter in this bind up. There will be <b>SPOILERS</b>, so please use caution in continuing if you have <i>not</i> read this graphic-novel or <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1644076193?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Vol. 1</a>!<br><br><b>
  <u>CHAPTER SEVEN:</u>
</b><br>We get to see Marko's past, the moon he grew up on, and how people started instilling the prejudice of wings very early in children's lives. Present day Marko is still in the tree space ship with Alana and their baby, Hazel, but the new additions are Marko's parents. Marko's mother has banished Izabel to another planet so he and his mother go after her, while Alana and Hazel stay in the ship with his father, who lets her in on a very important secret. <br><br><b>
  <u>CHAPTER EIGHT:</u>
</b><br>We get to see a glimpse of Alana and Marko first meeting - he was a prisoner and she was a guard. It wasn't exactly love at first sight, but I was still very appreciative of the glimpse. We learn that Marko's father, Barr, is an armorer. Then we see Marko's ex-girlfriend, Gwendolyn, looking for The Will. <br><br><b>
  <u>CHAPTER NINE:</u>
</b><br>The Will is taking The Stalk's death <i>very</i> hard. Gwendolyn finds him, promises to help him avenge The Stalk and helping him get back the young sex slave he was unable to save in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1644076193?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener">Vol. 1</a>. He desperately wants to kill Prince Robot IV, and agrees to start back up on his previous mission to find the half-breed baby once they rescue the young girl, who ends up having a pretty powerful ability. <br><br><b>
  <u>CHAPTER TEN:</u>
</b><br>We get to see Alana and Marko's relationship developing more in the prison. He smuggles her books, and she reads them to him. After Alana is informed that Marko is being sent to a new prison where the captives never come back, she takes action into her own hands and breaks him free. From there on out, they are on the run together. Back in our time, Marko and his mother find and save Izabel. Then, Gwendolyn and The Will are able to locate Marko and Alana thanks to the young girl they rescued. Gwendolyn is probably the most unstable ex-girlfriend of all time, and shoots a missile at their tree ship.<br><br><b>
  <u>CHAPTER ELEVEN:</u>
</b><br>We get to see Hazel being conceived, which was very humanizing. In present time, Marko's father sacrifices everything he has to protect the ship and his loved ones. Also, this issue kind of broke me, but my heart wasn't ready for Barr and then for the opener of the next chapter. <br><br><b>
  <u>CHAPTER TWELVE:</u>
</b><br>First Barr, now this rat medic? I felt my heart just being ripped out of my chest. Then, Prince Robot IV comes to Alana's favorite author's house. Thinking she will eventually show up to save him. Little does he know, the whole gang is already there and has been waiting for him. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1433872017i/15152636._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://meltotheany.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany/profile" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="3670002838211082451" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1134641631" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1134641631" />

        <a title="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘" href="/user/show/31461418-alienor-french-frowner">Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Alienor ✘ French Frowner ✘ by: </span>
      Kat Stark
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31461418-alienor-french-frowner?shelf=experiments">experiments</a>,

          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1134641631" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17156041229778199099"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423484248i/13631713._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b><u>Edit 06/14</u> : Reread before Volume 3</b> (always fucking fantastic)<br/><br/><i>Mesdames et Messieurs, I'm pleased to announce that... <b>this awesomeness of a book is my first 5-stars rating for a graphic novel! Prepare yourself for the love! </b></i><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423484248i/13631714._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>✭ <b>Remember how I was amazed by the storyline of the first Volume?</b> <i>Scratch that</i> : this one is even better. That's simple, we never seem to be able to breathe the whole time and the alternative POV bring more tension to the story, until we just <b>can't put it down</b>. Moreover, <b>Hazel</b></span>
  <span id="freeText17156041229778199099" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423484248i/13631713._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b><u>Edit 06/14</u> : Reread before Volume 3</b> (always fucking fantastic)<br><br><i>Mesdames et Messieurs, I'm pleased to announce that... <b>this awesomeness of a book is my first 5-stars rating for a graphic novel! Prepare yourself for the love! </b></i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423484248i/13631714._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>✭ <b>Remember how I was amazed by the storyline of the first Volume?</b> <i>Scratch that</i> : this one is even better. That's simple, we never seem to be able to breathe the whole time and the alternative POV bring more tension to the story, until we just <b>can't put it down</b>. Moreover, <b>Hazel's narration</b>, slightly ironic, allows us to see things differently - to produce a more complete picture of the consequences of those actions. I'm not going to lie, her comments cracked me up. Oh! And we get to learn how Marco and Alana met! How awesome is that? <br><br>✭ <i>What can I say?</i> <b>I'm in love with these characters</b>. First, <b>Alana</b>. Oh, this <i>wingy</i> could be my BBF : she's funny, brave, fierce, yet she loses her confidence sometimes (<i>what? Create a belly button can be scary!</i>) but never let someone belittle herself and the choices she made. As for <b>Marko</b>, well, is it bad if I'm a step away from adding him in my book boyfriend list? I know, <i>I know</i>, horns and all that stuff, but I can't help, he's all kind of adorable, naturally charming, and I found myself swooning more often than not. Yep. <i>Swooning</i>. If I had a couple of hours to write this review (<i>which I don't</i>), I'd add words and words to describe how much I enjoyed following Isabelle (best babysitter ever), The Will, his tentacles partner... But the only thing you need to know is the fact that <b>there isn't any useless character, as they all bring something fascinating to the story.</b><br><br>✭ <b>Let's talk about my favorite moments, shall we?</b> → Don't get fooled, the numbers here do not correspond to a rank or something like that : I'm fully unable to do something as accurate as a ranking, <i>duh</i>. <br><br>1) <b>Let's spread the love</b> with the <i>meet-cute</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423484248i/13631715._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>2) Feel the urge to <b>kill this Lying cat</b>.<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423484248i/13631716._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>3) The <b>reading scenes</b> : <i>yes, I'm a romantic like that.</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1420288952i/13200726.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>4) Of course, <b>the belly-button</b>. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423484248i/13631717._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>5) <b>Sexy Alana rocks</b>. <i>You know what I'm talking about.</i><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1401848383i/9857975.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>6) <b>The crazy mouse doctor</b>. I can't even explain clearly why I couldn't stop laughing, but well, I couldn't. <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1423484248i/13631718._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Well. I have to stop here otherwise I'll tell you the entire story. I guess you just have to read it to find out.<br><br><i>For more of my reviews, please visit:</i><br><blockquote>
  <a href="https://meetthebookworld.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1487851828i/22057164._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote></span>

<div id="review_2377495071" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2377495071" />
    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2377495071?book_show_action=true">Apr 30, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2377495071" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8352681784903390862">Originally, I had planned to read this second volume not before May (the end of May to be exact) but after reading volume one yesterday and having both here at home in paperback form ... I just couldn't resist.<br/><br/>This tells of Marko's parents being on the tree rocketship (have I mentioned I want one?) and how that affects everyone. They thought Marko had been kidnapped, then find out the truth ... and aren't happy. Especially not his mother.<br/>Nevertheless, they come around (sort of, for now) and the </span>
  <span id="freeText8352681784903390862" style="display:none">Originally, I had planned to read this second volume not before May (the end of May to be exact) but after reading volume one yesterday and having both here at home in paperback form ... I just couldn't resist.<br /><br />This tells of Marko's parents being on the tree rocketship (have I mentioned I want one?) and how that affects everyone. They thought Marko had been kidnapped, then find out the truth ... and aren't happy. Especially not his mother.<br />Nevertheless, they come around (sort of, for now) and the patchwork family sticks together, if only out of necessity since the enemies keep coming. This time, while there is one bounty hunter less, there is also Marko's former fiancée who (understandably) wants her rings back and is so not cool with how their relationship ended.<br /><br />There aren't as many crazy different places this takes place but we learn more about the rocketship and interpersonal relationships (like how Alana and Marko met or scenes from Marko's childhood and Prince IV's war-time experiences) and it helps to build connections. It also makes evident that the author is not afraid to really punch the reader in the gut or address the big topics. On the contrary, I suspect we will delve deeper into the uncomfortable-or-even-hurtful-but-true territory as the story unfolds in future volumes.<br /><br />The art, once again, is as weird as the creatures in this universe and as pretty as the inside of the rocketship, with every kind of colour you can imagine and depicting EVERYTHING in great detail (even the icky bits one never wanted to see *lol*).</span>
  <a data-text-id="8352681784903390862" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('bJSlAo9x2yQgU5WeZmtNB+Nh3t6MacxJ+FMF+1azk5nbTvZjeJS1FMLS4fxTS+bcTpBSm16/vOQXqITFq0rn+A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('p5ncVZc0pb7aGCqUcWg4iqyG2XP4xj8+Kqu+dzhsRQcQQ480YNHLjjiZXvZESJNRAXdVNioQT5PFUD9JxZUxZg==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer17938102688355907601">Brian K. Vaughan is the writer and co-creator of comic-book series including SAGA, PAPER GIRLS, Y THE LAST MAN, RUNAWAYS, and most recently, BARRIER, a digital comic with artist Marcos Martin about immigration, available from their pay-what-you-want site <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='http://www.PanelSyndicate.com'>www.PanelSyndicate.com</a><br/><br/>BKV's work has been recognized at the Eisner, Harvey, Hugo, Shuster, Eagle, and British Fantasy Awards. He sometimes writes</span>
  <span id="freeText17938102688355907601" style="display:none">Brian K. Vaughan is the writer and co-creator of comic-book series including SAGA, PAPER GIRLS, Y THE LAST MAN, RUNAWAYS, and most recently, BARRIER, a digital comic with artist Marcos Martin about immigration, available from their pay-what-you-want site <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.PanelSyndicate.com">www.PanelSyndicate.com</a><br /><br />BKV's work has been recognized at the Eisner, Harvey, Hugo, Shuster, Eagle, and British Fantasy Awards. He sometimes writes for film and television in Los Angeles, where he lives with his family and their dogs Hamburger and Milkshake. </span>
